text:
Hey everyone! I'm the person that posted this recipe and I appreciate all the feedback (good and bad) along with what everyone did to make it their own. I read over some of the recommendations, and this is what I did to make this recipe even better. I replaced the water with Pepsi, added about a tsp of liquid smoke, and seasoned the ribs with a rub of salt, pepper, garlic powder, onion powder and brown sugar. Added the onion and garlic as stated in the recipe, and cooked them on high for just under 4 hours and followed the rest of the directions. With these changes, I love the recipe even more (though as many people have stated, it's pretty excellent as written)! I know that many people love them to 'fall off the bone', but good ribs should still have a nice bite and pull when you bite into them. Adjust the cooking time accordingly, but for my slow cooker, they are cooked perfectly between 3.5 and 4 hours. Thanks again for all the feedback!! ~Norah

text:
I was really skeptical about ribs in a slow cooker, so I tried this recipe twice to make sure that the first time wasn't a fluke.  I am a convert, that's for sure.  These were amazing! First time, I made it exactly as the recipe called for and these ribs were fall off the bone good.  The second time, I added smoked paprika and garlic powder to the rub on the ribs before I put them in the slow cooker.  I also used 1/2 cup of beer instead of the water (any liquid will add flavour).  I cooked them on high in the slow cooker for 3 hours and 45 minutes.  I covered a 9 x 11 baking dish with tin foil (to help with clean up) and put the ribs in the uncovered baking dish.  I coated the ribs with bbq sauce and put them in the oven at 350F for 20 minutes.  I pulled the ribs out and added another thin layer of bbq sauce before putting them back in the oven under the broiler for 7 to 10 minutes to get that crust on the top.  The ribs were perfect.  My family thanks you for this recipe which I will be using again and again!  Amanda

Slow cooking makes the difference here.  Instead of finishing in the oven, I basted with sauce and placed them on a medium-heat grill for 15-20 minutes.  Turn every 5 minutes and baste the meaty side 1-2 more times until desired level of caramelization (is that a word?).  Great recipe! We will use it every time we make ribs.

text:
This is an excellent "cheater" recipe for the most part.  Still, it fell from perfection because the cooking time was too long. Hubs and I do far too much rib eating in our travels and one thing we've learned from the experts is that, contrary to popular belief, you don't WANT your ribs to fall off the bone.  If that's the state they end up in they've been cooked too long (or stewed).  We like our ribs tender, yet with the meat still clinging to the bone.  I cooked them just short of 4 hours on high, and if I do this again I'd shorten that by an hour.  The finish in the oven, however, was just right - 15 minutes at 375 degrees resulted in a sticky, caramelized,  glazed exterior.  I didn't bother with either the onion or garlic, but I did season them with a good rub seasoning a few hours before I started them in the Crock Pot.  The bottom line?  In spite of not being smoked or grilled, and in spite of too long a stint in the Crock Pot, these were some "D" fine ribs.

text:
Great recipe. Based on other reviews, i modified a bit. seasoned the ribs w/ a pork rub then place on grill for a few minutes on each side to sear (this will help keep some of the juices in). Placed in crockpot on high for 3 hrs and used 1/2 cup of beer instead of water (I've heard coke works great too). Didn't bother w/ the onion and garic. Then finished off in the oven for 10 minutes on each side w/ sauce to caramalize. Very tender and bone came right out when eating. 
P.S. It never mentioned how to put the ribs in the crockpot...After research I placed them on their side (Thicker end down and meaty side facing out). Worked great.

text:
Love the recipe, but just wanted to throw out a little warning...make sure not to overfill the crock pot.  Probably a beginner mistake, but wanted to leave a note for any other beginners.

This was my 2nd time using this recipe.  The first time turned out great, but this time I overdid it and used 6 slabs of ribs when the max for my crock pot probably should be 4.

The ribs tasted great, but some of them had meat falling off the bone while others we had to work for.  Could have been a a coincidence with just a different quality meat (which happens sometime), but I noticed some inconsistency in how the meat was cooking in the crock pot.

Again, probably a "rookie mistake", but just wanted to pass it on for any others that are new to using a crock pot.  Once it gets warm, I'm going back to the grill, but until then, this recipe will get the job done...as long as I stick to the directions!

text:
First off I'd like to say that I have been making all types of ribs all different types of ways for years. I love doing them in my smoker  and my grill using indirect method but I was wanting to learn a quicker way using my crock pot so I tried this recipe and I was pleasantly surprised by just how tasty, quick and easy this is compared to other ways that I do. I never really thought that ribs could actually be done in a crock pot and taste or have the consistency that we are used to. I have a rather large crock pot so I used one cup of water and one cup of apple cider vinegar, then I added some onion and garlic for the ribs to sit on as well as for flavor,then I rubbed the ribs with   salt,black pepper,garlic powder,onion powder,paprika,brown sugar and a little Old Bay. I almost forgot to say I also removed the white membrane from the underside of the ribs before applying the rub. I then set the ribs on top of onion/garlic and topped with more onion and garlic. Cooked on high for 3.75 hours and then put into a baking pan,applied my own bbq sauce and baked for 25 minutes (under the broiler for the last 5 minutes or so) They were "stupid good!" Also crock pots like ovens vary in temperature so use any recipe as a guideline, do not think they are written in stone. Also ribs come in various thicknesses as they are from an animal not created in a lab and have varying degrees of fat and these things will also effect cooking times. Thank you very much for posting!!

text:
I've made ribs this way a few times. Maybe it's my slow cooker but I've found it takes less time than the original recipe calls for, I guess you need to know your equipment. As soon as the ends of the bones begin to stick out from the meat, I know they're done. Any more and they'll totally fall apart. Finish them off in the oven OR on the grill (low heat) and you'll have delicious, falling-off-the-bone ribs every time. Try a spice rub first, experiment with different BBQ sauces until you get it to your liking.

text:
I have made these slow cooker ribs 4 times now and they are a HIT with a picky 16 year-old who now requests them every week! I season them with garlic powder and a touch of ground cinnamon (not too much) in addition to the salt and pepper. I have some good tips for coating the ribs with the barbecue sauce before putting them into the oven. I place about half the bottle of barbecue sauce in an oblong, plastic bowl and thin out the sauce with about 1/4 cup of water---not too runny, though (use a little bit of water at a time). Using tongs, I then place one portion of ribs into the sauce bowl to coat them with sauce one portion at a time (I always cut my rack of ribs into 2 or 3 rib portions before seasoning and cooking them in the crock pot). Using the tongs, I carefully slide each portion around the sauce bowl and a spoon to baste hard to reach areas with sauce to make sure it is very well coated. I then place the portion onto a foil-lined baking pan (makes for easier clean up). They always come out great! Thanks for such a wonderful recipe. :)

I thought that the ribs were excellent. Followed the recipe as is, except that along with the salt/pepper called for in the recipe, I added brown sugar, onion powder and garlic powder (to taste) to the rub.  Poured Diet Coke into the slow cooker instead of water and cooked on high for exactly 4 hrs.  Conducting a little taste test, I coated half of the ribs with Sweet Billy Ray's BBQ sauce and the other ribs with Safeway store brand BBQ sauce and baked for 20 minutes.  Safeway won! The meat was tender, succulent and melted in my mouth without senselessly falling off the bone when being handled. After all, the fun in eating ribs is taking the meat off the bone with your MOUTH!

text:
Turn this recipe into 5 stars by using it as a great base recipe for you to experiment using your own likes and flavors. 

For me, I like to start off with a dry rub of salt,  course ground pepper, garlic powder, onion powder, crushed red peppers or paprika, and brown suger. (You can forego the salt if you use garlic salt or onion salt)

Instead of plain ole water use a Coke, Dr. Pepper, Beer, or broth. (I love Dr. Pepper so I use that)

Cut the rib racks into slabs of 5 to 6 ribs each. Cover the ribs generously with the dry rub and layer them with the onions and minced garlic into the slow cooker.

Follow the cooking directions in the recipe. (4 hours on high or 8 hours on low)

I prefer to finish the ribs on the grill instead of in the oven. It gives the ribs a good char.

After reading some reviews and then the original posters tweeks to the recipe, I made it basically the way she did after altering the recipe with a only minor exceptions:  I rubbed the ribs with a combination of salt, pepper, and garlic.  I didn't have onion powder on hand.  I let that sit overnight and then cooked it in a 1/2c water and about a tbsp of liquid smoke with slices of onion.  I cooked on high for 3 3/4hrs, took out and placed in baking pan then lathered in bbq sauce (I used Jack Daniels Hickory brown sugar).  I baked at 350 for 15 min.  I poured more bbq sauce on and cooked about another 5 minutes.  My son loves ribs and he thought these were very good.  I'm not crazy about ribs, especially the hours it takes to grill or smoke so for me this was easy and they were very tasty.

text:
I made these per the recipe, and offer these suggestions. First, 8 hrs on low was far too long, at least for my crock pot. 6-6.5 would have been better. I struggled to get them out of the crock pot in one piece at 7.5. Definitely the first time I've had to eat ribs with a fork.  Second, season them in the crock before you cook. Even after simmering in garlic and onion, the meat didn't have much flavor. And third, baste both sides of the ribs with sauce, even though you only caramelize them on one side. You'll appreciate having the sauce flavor in every bite.

I followed some of the other reviewers suggestions and seasoned the ribs over night. I used a BBQ spice blend and a few other seasoning's (garlic powder, salt, Dijon mustard and paprika) and I am so glad that did, it really bumped up the flavour factor. The ribs do not need any longer then 3.5 to 4 hrs for cooking, they were delicious and I can't wait to make this again for more people, if you want to impress someone I suggest you give these a try.

text:
I basically followed the contributor's updated recipe trying to use things I already had at home because I was in a hurry to get the ribs into the slow cooker. No Pepsi but a small can of Coke worked. I rubbed them with salt, pepper, some chili powder and brown sugar. Cut the whole rack in three sections and overlaid them in the slow cooker, putting the onion and garlic on top. They cooked on low for about 7 hours. I removed the ribs to a foil-covered baking sheet, slathered them with BBQ sauce and baked for 15 minutes. They were fall-off-the-bone delicious! This will definitely be my go-to recipe when it's too cold to grill outside.

text:
Awesome recipe.  Thanks for sharing.  I eliminated the 1/2 cup water, and used 1/2 pineapple juice instead.  I marinated the ribs overnight in a giant ziplock bag with pineapple juice, garlic, and onions.

Then, I skipped adding the BBQ sauce, and instead just put the ribs in the oven for 10 minutes, then just dipped a few ribs in BBQ sauce while I ate them.  But they were great without the BBQ sauce too.

Real BBQ, as you'd get in a well-established rib joint in Memphis, are served without sauce.  Then they put a big selection of BBQ sauces on the table.  After all, BBQ is a style of cooking, it's not the sauce.

I love ribs - one of my all time go to faves, but hate the prices in a restaurant. I learned how to slow roast them in the oven, which is good, but sometimes too warm in always sunny So Cal. I bought a fixer-upper a few years ago. The kitchen was original circa 1955 and nothing worked, but one single induction burner on the cook top. So I've relied on my slow cooker quite a bit as I've refurbished my home. I was shocked and so excited to find this recipe. 
I made it exactly as stated and the ribs came out perfectly - I finished them on my outdoor grill - some BBQ sauce and a nice flame - WOW!!
Even after a fully working kitchen, my go to cook method for ribs is my trusty crock pot.

Made this looking for an easy work day/school day /practice day meal. The family was pretty shocked at how good it was because we are pretty big fans of  bbq'd ribs. This is definitely a keeper. We prepared two racks of ribs (with seasonings, two cap fulls of apple cider vinegar, beer and a couple drops of liquid smoke ) in the crockpot and left overnight in the fridge. city:

None
text:
I really enjoyed the ribs but I found that you can get rid of the bland boiled meat flavour if you add the barbeque sauce at the beginning when you put the ribs in the slow cooker. But make sure not to use the full bottle at first, so you still have some sauce left to put on top of the ribs before you put them on a baking sheet and in the oven. This allows you to skip the step of marinating the ribs overnight.
Also, note that the longer you cook the ribs in the oven, the more dried out they will get. I found that 15 min in the oven was a little too long, but this was easily fixed by just putting the ribs back in the hot slow cooker (with all the liquid still in it) for another 5-10 min to make the meat more tender again.
Also, for those of you who are unsure about cooking the meat from frozen, don't worry about it. I had no problems and I used ribs that were straight from the freezer.
Great base recipe but needs a little tweak. Thanks!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Rubbed 2 slabs of ribs with 1/2 cup brown sugar, 1/8 tsp pepper, sprinkle of salt, 1/2 tsp of onion powder and garlic powder.  B est to give it time to marinate a few hours or  overnight, but it will be okay if you don't have time.

Sliced one onion and layered it and sprinkled minced clove of garlic over each piece.

Used one can of coke rather than water, like suggested and added a tablespoon of liquid smoke.   I put this in the bottom of the slow cooker and then put the rubbed ribs in it.

I have cooked it high for 4 hours and low for 8 hours - both turned out tasty.   If you want the bones still on,  don't cook it too long.  It doesn't effect the taste or tenderness, but if you cook too long, it will fall off the bones.  Some people like like it like that,but I prefer to have the bones on.

Baking it with barbeque sauce adds that final touch. of yumminess.

I used to boil, then bake, then barbeque the ribs and that was a tedious, time consuming and messy process.  This is a much simpler and equally great tasting batch of ribs.

text:
I have to add my two cents to everyone else's review - EXCELLENT!!! After reading just about every review I decided to take the plunge (I am not known for ribs. HAHA)
I took some others' suggestions and marinated the ribs in red wine vinegar, Worcestershire sauce and soy sauce (just mix to taste), then rubbed the ribs with smoked paprika and garlic powder before putting them in the slow cooker. 
I also chose High (4 hours), as others suggested, and they cooked up PERFECTLY - very tender, but stayed intact until we bit into them. I think the 8 hours would have made them fall apart.
Another suggestion I took was to use 1/2 cup of beer instead of water. It was delicious, but I think I'll use beef broth next time. The hint of beer was fine - just not my thing. You may love that touch, so don't be afraid to try it.
I have never been able to make ribs before, but this is now my "go-to" recipe!!!!

Just ok for us...these are a little more greasy than those done on the grill.  Definitely marinate the ribs in a dry rub for 24 hours prior to cooking - that's a must if possible!  They are pretty bland as written (I used onion powder, garlic powder, regular paprika, salt and pepper rub per the reviews prior to cooking but did not let them marinate... also used the beer in place of the water and added a tbsp of liquid smoke which really didn't seem to make a difference...no smoky taste really.)  I think if I made these again, I would finish them off on the grill.  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
I followed a few of the other "twists" to this recipe and, with a brown sugar/fresh cracked pepper/garlic powder and Johnny's Seasoning Salt (it is my go-to seasoning...from the Pacific NW) leaving it to absorb all of these spices overnight then into the crockpot they went.  I used the original recipe creator's suggestion of Pepsi instead of water, added some chopped onions, minced garlic and let them go for 4 hours on HIGH...think that is key, as well.  When I removed them they were still very well intact, just ready to fall off the bone, so draining the liquid and finishing with Sweet Baby Rays with a few dashes of Liquid Smoke in the oven at 350 for an hour, uncovered produced a HEAVENLY, tender rib!  Thank you, Norah, for a lovely recipe, and for being so forgiving to those of us that have tweaked it a bit.

text:
This is a good recipe.  If you want your ribs faster, you can cut the ribs into 2 or 3 rib sections.  Add salt, pepper, onion etc. to each section and wrap individually in foil.  Place the pieces, seam side up, in a roasting pan (doesn't matter if you stack them on top of each other) and bake at 275 degrees for 2-3 hours.  Then remove them and continue with this recipe in the oven, basting with bbq sauce.

text:
In order to minimize grease, you can put them under your broiler 5 to 10 min. per side.  I like to cut ribs into serving size to make it easer loading the crock pot.  If you add 1/2 tsp or so of liquid smoke to the bbq sauce, it will make ribs taste like they were done on the grill.  I don't bother with the oven or grill to carmelize as we like them so tender right out of the pot.

text:
Followed much of the advice in the reviews... 

1) Rubbed the ribs with garlic powder, onion powder, brown sugar, salt, and pepper... wrapped them and stuck in fridge overnight
2) Used Dr Pepper instead of water and layered the onions between the rib slabs starting with the onions on bottom
3) Cooked on low for 6 hours (because I out of the house) 
4) Brushed them with a good BBQ sauce and finished in the oven for 20 min or so.

Very tasty, but too falling off the bone.  Even on low six hours is too long in a newer slow cooker as manufacturers have recently upped the heat at every setting.

text:
I followed Norah's revised recipe: Used 1/2 cup beer instead of water; used the rub on the ribs prior to placing in crock pot- salt, pepper, garlic powder, onion powder and brown sugar. Did not use liquid smoke as I did not have and didn't miss. Cooked on high for 3 hr 45 min and then placed in a 350 degree oven- after adding bar-b-que sauce. After 20 minutes put under broiler for 10 minutes. Flavor was fantastic. Loved that the meat was still attached to the bones. Not overwhelming bar-b-que sauce that happens when adding that from the get go in the crock pot. Super recipe! Look forward to cooking again!

text:
We dont do ribs very often, but bought a large pack at Costco, and fixed half of them  the usual way - boiled for a couple of hours then finished them on the grill. They were kind of tough so threw the other half in the freezer & forget about them. Decided to clean out the freezer & debated how to fix the second half since they were frozen solid. I thought Id give the crockpot method a try. I cooked on high for 4 1/2 hours, but used a bottle of beer instead of water and followed the rest of the recipe. They were very tender and turned out awesome! I think we will have to make them more than once or twice a year now!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Loved these with the following changes:  Made rub out of  
1 and  t cumin, 1 T paprika, 1 T garlic powder, 1 T onion powder, 1  t chili powder, 2 T light brown sugar, 1 T sea salt, 1/2 t cayenne pepper, 1 t black pepper, 1 t dry mustard powder. After removing membrane, rubbed ribs and let sit overnight in fridge. Cooked in slow cooker in regular coca cola (not water) for 3.75 hours on high.  Left out onion and garlic as that is in the rub.   Preheat oven to 375 degrees F (190 degrees C), transfer ribs to a baking sheet. Pat dry. Coat ribs with barbeque sauce. (I used Sweet Baby Rays Sweet n Spicy). Bake in preheated oven for 20 min; flip halfway through. Changed to high broiler for 4 minutes; make sure you do not go over and burn ribs.
Absolutely everyone wanted more of these!  Thank you for sharing your recipe. Will make these again and again...

text:
Finally getting around to reviewing this. I've made this twice. The first time, 6 hours on low which was way too long and I ruined it. WATCH your slow cooker. You want the rib meat to start to pull away from the bone. A fork should go in, but not separate it from the bone. Then, take it out, put sauce on and bake it 350 until your desired doneness. For me, that was 4 hours in the slow cooker and 30 mins at 350. That knowledge came from the second try. I won't do ribs any other way.  Instead of the 1/2 cup of water, I used soda. Cherry cola this 2nd time. THANK you very much for this excellent cheat!  **Third time the charm. All the same as above, but salted the ribs one day ahead which acts as a dry brine. Wonderful...and thank you again.**

text:
I've been making ribs in the slow cooker for years.  Over time, I've refined a recipe that never fails.  Before  placing in the crock pot,  a simple dry rub to add flavor.  Instead of water, try a can ok coke or Dr. Pepper.  This tenderizes the meat and adds a sweet flavor.  Instead of placing the ribs in the oven, I char them on the grill over a high direct flame. Add BBQ sauce, turn flame to med 5 min before removing from the grill.

text:
I made it, along with the author's changes, and it was fabulous.  Took off the membrane on the back, gave it a rub of minced garlic, paprika, salt and pepper, some cajun seasonings. Cut up a whole white onion, placed in the bottom of the crockpot.  Put the meat in, meat side down. Poured over 3/4 cup Foster's ale and heated for 1 1/2 hours high. Then I did another couple hrs on low.  Took the ribs out, put on a baking sheet with foil. Spread BBQ sauce over the ribs and popped in the oven at 400 for about 20 minutes. Served with mashed potatoes. Scooped up the onions still floating i the slow cooker, and put them over the potatoes with butter. Heaven.

text:
This method made bottom of the barrel ribs taste good! First I did a homemade rib rub overnight then  I used a can of ginger ale for 2 packs of ribs and put some BQ sauce on them and cooked on high for about 4 hours. Then I threw more BQ sauce on and more spices and put in oven for about 20 minutes. 
Update: I may just skip the slowcooker next time. I made these again and they seemed a bit overcooked rather than tender. This time I did a rub (brown sugar, chili powder, garlic powder, onion powder, salt, pepper) for the ribs, left on about 30 mins before I put in oven at 400 degrees for 15 mins per side. Then I slathered on honey and added more spices and bq sauce, poured apple juice in slowcooker and cooked it for about 3.5 hrs on high. I added more spice and BQ sauce throughout. I had so many ribs I had to cook some in oven, which I did at 275 degs for same length of time wrapped in foil. Then after I added mixture of honey, spices and BQ sauce I carmelized all for 10 mins. All were good but ribs that stayed in oven whole time were very tender and juicy.

text:
This was my very first time making ribs in my life - EVER - and they turned out beautifully!  I altered this recipe by putting the garlic and onion in the bottom of the crock (lined it first with a crock liner) and using Coke instead of water.  Otherwise, I followed it exactly. 

A note for other first-timers: perhaps this is common but I didn't know to expect it: the ribs were GREY after being in the crock pot for 4 hours.  But after I put the barbecue sauce on them and baked them (on a foil-lined baking sheet), they looked exactly like ribs *should*, and tasted delicious.

I probably should have cooked mine a bit longer, since the meat was tender but not falling off the bone as I like it.  Still, they were really delicious.  The only other change is that I added a bit more chopped garlic than called for and a few dashes of worcestershire sauce to the coke, since I read in other comments that it was included in some marinades. I bet soy would have been delicious, too!

Served with cole slaw and baked beans.  Thanks for a great recipe - I will definitely be making this again!

I don't have a girll so this was a recipe I was looking for. These ribs are amazing. I read all the reviews and when I saw the review that the chef put on here saying they revised it I had to try it that way. I rubbed the ribs in the salt, pepper, garlic salt and brown sugar. Put it into the crock pit with the soda, garlic and onion. I left my crock pot on low because I was going to be gone last four hours. I followed the directions exactly after they were done. However, I did not throw out the onions or the juice. I out the onions on the baking sheet with the ribs and covered in BBQ sauce. Then I threw the baking sheet in the oven for 15.with the juice I made gravy for the side of mashed potatoes   The onions were AMAZING!!  Don't waste those opinions. They were sweet and crystallized like the ribs.The gravy was outstanding. I did add some beef bouillon to it before I made the gravy. The rib meat was perfect. Thank you for this recipe I will forever use this. Even if I do get a grill someday.

text:
1. Seasoning ribs with garlic salt, paprika, pepper, seal in the hot saucepan until both sides brown.
2. Add 2 TBSP vinigar in the slow cook along with water, onion, garlic and rib, cook 8 hours in low or 4 hours in high.
3. Move the ribs out of slow cook, brush BBQ sauce on the rib, put in oven at 375 bake 8 mins, turn over, brush BBQ sause , bake another 7 min.

These were so good and so easy! I'm rating this with my changes in mind. I used cider vinegar and chicken broth instead of the water. I also added a TBL of liquid smoke, Worcester sauce, and a1/4 cup of barbecue sauce. I also seasoned the ribs with garlic powder, onion powder, a little cayenne pepper for a kick, fresh ground black pepper, a little sea salt. I cooked on low 8 hours on low in crockpot. text:
This is a perfect base recipe, and becomes a five star recipe when you use the modifications suggested by the OG poster, or others. The method is perfect: 3.5 hours on high had these ribs ready to eat, I might even try less time next time, or cooking on low, for a bit more bite to my ribs. The water doesn't seem like much, and other recipes suggest "adding enough liquid to cover" but it wasn't necessary at all. I put this thicker rib sections on the bottom and the thinner layered on top and everything worked out fine. I used the onion/garlic/broth mixture leftover as the liquid in "A Very Popular BBQ Sauce" which is another recipe on this site (posted by JRNEUMILLER). Why let it go to waste? It was quick to prepare and left me with more than enough sauce for the next batch.

text:
Awesome!   I couldn't believe how easy it is to make baby back ribs.   

Mentioning the delicious ribs to someone they asked, "did you boil them? ... Did you grill them on low?...did you..."  Dare I share that all I did was cut them in sizes to fit in crockpot (2 layers), added onion & garlic? pour in 1 cup beer, seasoned  with salt/pepper, put on low for 6-8 hrs.   The meat appeared to be  falling off the bone!

I used a metal spatula to transfer them to cookie sheet (covered in aluminum foil and nonstick spray for easy clean up).  Basted bbq sauce on both sides, cook 375 for 8 min, baste again with BBQ sauce, 8 minutes in oven...>>> Done and delicious!

My household ate them;  including my 2 and 4 year old!  Enjoy!

My boys don't really like messy food much, but since I've been sick they've had to endure a number of easy dinners. Now that I'm on the mend, I decided to try these ribs for a real Sunday night dinner. I followed the suggestions of the original author, rubbed the ribs and cooked them in Pepsi, then popped them in the oven with the BBQ sauce on.  I did 15 minutes on each side, and would probably have increased that to 20 on each side at 375, or do the 15/15 split, then turn up the broiler for a minute or two. Really tasty, I highly recommend them, and the boys ate them with no problem - messy fingers and all.

text:
Please do yourself a favor and make this recipe!  So easy and basically no mess nor fuss. Somethings to note though:  1.)  You will need to season the ribs BEFORE you put them in the slow cooker.  The meat needs salt, pepper, and whatever other staples on your spice rack.  2.)  Use something other than water as your liquid.  I used a Pepsi and it really helped add that special something to the meat.  I would use a Pepsi again, and would try it with beer, or a liquid smoke/water mix.  3.)  Like some of the reviewers mentioned, 4 hours on High is waaay too long.  I checked mine at 3 hours and they were just right - could cut them with the edge of a fork!!  Any longer and they would have shredded.  4.)  The oven option is a must.  This will give you the sticky sauce your looking for when you eat ribs.  Happy cooking!

text:
Used frozen boneless ribs I got on sale and had stored in the freezer.  Sprayed very lightly to make dry ingedients stick and coated ea. with a rib rub.  Also added a tsp. of liquid smoke and half an onion, sliced.
Cooked on high for an hour, then 5hrs. on low.  In my cooker, they were almost ready to fall apart by then.
Bonus:  I could not stand the thought of just tossing out that beautiful stock that was left after cooking.  Poured it into a batter bowl and refrigerated to get the fat to the top.  It made a jellied broth with a thick layer of fat on top.  Kept about 2 T. of the fat (for extra flavor) and tossed the rest.  After that just used the fat with Smart Balance, flour, milk, and a lot of the broth to make a lot of tasty gravy.  Yum.
Delicious.  Great recipe.

I basically did everything EXCEPT the night before I plan to cook them I buy a rub and put it all over the ribs and wrap them in saran wrap. I let them sit in the fridge like that over night then the next morning I cook them in the crock pot on high for about 5-5.5 hours and then turn it on low for another 2 hours. I broil the ribs for about 7-14 (varies on the size!) And it gets them crispy like on the grill! Just really watch them!!!

text:
I usually seared the meat first, but I'm glad I tried this recipe, I love how BBQ sauce caramelized in the oven at the end, and the meat was so tender. I made some changes to the recipe though. I dry brine the meat by rubbing kosher salt all over and leaving it in the fridge over night. I made spice rub with black pepper, smoked paprika, garlic powder and cayenne and rub it before putting in the slow cooker. I also sprinkled liquid smoke on the meat. I sliced a whole onion and laid them on the bottom, did not add any liquid. I placed pork meat side down, bone side up and slather some BBQ sauce on the top. I cooked for a little over four hours in the slow cooker, slather more BBQ sauce, and finished in the 400F oven for 10 minutes.

I always try a new dish using my crock pot because it's very convenient to use and it's wonderful to come home to an aromatic house and dinner waiting at home.

I tried this tonight and it turned out better than I thought.  The meat usually turns out way too dry whenever I have made them in the crockpot (and it could be something I'm doing wrong, I don't know).  Despite my previous mishaps with any type of meat that I've made in the crockpot turning out very, very dry (albeit, falling off the bone, whether it's chicken or pork), I've never made baby back ribs so I thought I would give this a try and I'm glad I did!

I followed the directions just as it was instructed, with some additions of my own, like adding largely chopped potatoes, carrots and slices of apples.  I didn't discard the onions because they came out so tasty and tender that we ate them as part of our side dish.  The only thing that didn't taste well was our barbeque sauce.  It wasn't too sweet at all.  I'll be using a different barbeque sauce next time.  But, nonetheless, this recipe will be a keeper, for sure!  Thank you for this recipe

I pretty much followed the recipe exactly.  At 3 1/2 hours on high with the slow cooker, I needed to run an errand.  Not wanting the ribs to cook another hour on high, I turned it down to low.  I could see they were done at that point, and fall off the bone tender.  They cooked another 90 minutes or so on low, then I finished them in the oven as instructed. They were perfect, so good and so easy!  I've never made ribs before and these were the highlight of my 4th of july dinner.  Better than the king crab legs.  I had found a 3 minute video on you tube showing how to trim them, that helped.  I will definitely make these again, so delicious and what could be easier.

I read a lot of reviews before trying these today. The only other time I tried ribs in the slow cooker they fell off the bone which was not what I was going for.  I put a rub on the ribs last night. I used the rub on this site. I used chicken broth instead of water and added the tbsp of liquid smoke. I cooked them on high for 3:45 minutes. Put BBQ sauce on them and baked at 375* for 15 minutes. text:
I have a recipe similar to this but instead of using water, I use apple juice concentrate, the frozen kind, along with a little water added to cover the meat entirely.  I also rub the ribs liberally with pork rub and make sure to remove the membrane from the bone side of the ribs.  Also, before finishing them in the oven I pull the bones out of the meat so you are left with completely boneless ribs ready to be eaten with little or no mess.  I finish with a spicy barbecue sauce so the sweetness of the apple juice is a nice contrast.  Very good overall.  Instead of apple juice concentrate I have experimented with jams and jellies as well.  Plum jelly mixed with water is a great flavor for ribs.

text:
I love this recipe. They were tender and Here are my notes:
--I totally agree with marinating them overnight. I used Worcestershire, soy sauce (low sodium), minced garlic, pepper, and smoked paprika. I would have added some of the other things folks posted, but didn't have them all. 
--I cooked them in the crock pot for 3 hr. 50 minutes (on high). Shortening it under four hours does seem to keep the meat on the bone, but still tender.
--Fifteen minutes in the oven is perfect. 
--I used a rub on the ribs and let them sit for about 15 minutes while the oven pre-heated. 
--I reserved some of the bar-b-q sauce from the bottle and heated it to serve on the side with the ribs. 
--I served them with mashed potatoes and green beans.
